Making small mistakes or sending messages that make no sense is the way to go if you want to prevent detection. Throwing off the scent. For example, simple spelling errors can make a huge problem. Or, you use jargon for certain words. Because finding a key is tied to the entire message as a whole usually. For example, you can take some binary code 110010110101. Now, shift it just one place left or right, you get the entirely different information that might not contain any useful information at all as a whole, but if you look at certain segments it might. But you are NOT looking at segments, you are looking at a whole thing trying to find a key.  Long story short, when you know the key, that little "mistake" is invisible. You get thou instead of though, for example. But when you DON'T know the code and you look at it as a whole, it makes the figuring out of the key nearly impossible. So those shorter ones? They could hold some information... or they could simply be a ruse.  Imagine German Enigma code - and that Germans had the habit of entering some gibberish once in a while. Just random letters. You start decoding with the key you think is right, and all of a sudden some nonsense comes along. You say "Oh well, this key is wrong, only some words make sense, must be something different" and you move forward. Just like they found gas chamber on that one try that was actually wrong.  It is a masterful way to hide the information... but it only makes sense to use it to hide two way communication when both sides know the key. Boasting to someone by expecting them to figure out you've made a mistake on purpose... that's not really it. Mistake was, in this case, probably a non intentional one.

5:13 You don't say...
You know, the pulling up behind another vehicle and turning on your high-beams to blind the occupants (as it was said the Zodiac did to the 19 and 22-year old couple) is a very specific technique taught and regularly practiced by law enforcement...and basically no one else. That's why cops blind the occupants of a car with their high-beams and spotlights after pulling them over almost every time. It's as much to help the cop see in as it is prevent the occupants from seeing out, and puts things in the cop's favor big time should there be an exchange of gunfire.  And while the concept of 'a bright light can blind you' is something we all understand without being taught it, the thought of using your car's high beams as a force multiplier that works in both an offensive and defensive capacity like that isn't going to just pop into your head out of no where...at least I don't think it would. I think most people would have to be taught it or seen it/something like it done before they'd think to do something like that themselves  And that small detail of him flashing on his brights to set off the ambush is just one more teeny-tiny hint among many suggesting he was/had been, in law enforcement. Maybe I'm over-thinking it. But hey, that's part of the fun of researching things like this, right? =) He was a cop!

The killer took pride in his work and passively mocked law enforcement and how "simplistic" they, bold in his confidence to call them just around the block. So maybe for the remaining ciphers, think complex, or beyond reasonable understanding. *If you're new here* -----  The Zodiac Killer is the pseudonym of an American serial killer who operated in Northern California from at least the late 1960s to the early 1970s. The unidentified killer originated the name in a series of taunting letters and cards sent to the San Francisco Bay Area press. These letters included four cryptograms.
